work</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">The kinetic analysis of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C through CV curves was explored to understand the in-depth reason of the outstanding electrochemical performances. As shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a,b for CV curves at 0.1, 0.3, 0.5, 0.7, 1.5, 3.0, 5.0, and 7.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, the weak peak at 1.6 V was included in the distinct oxidation peak at 1.7 V; meanwhile, three reduction ones were obvious at each curves, greatly coinciding with the discharge–charge platforms. In addition, the similar shapes of each curves again verified the weak polarization. According to the previous reports, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48 ref49 ref50 ref51 ref52 ref53" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref48 ref49 ref50 ref51 ref52 ref53" aria-label="reference 48 to 53">(48−53)</a> the equations as following were used to explore the kinetic behavior in detail.<span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq1"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i11"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq2"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_m002.gif" alt="" id="_i12"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(2)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq3"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_m003.gif" alt="" id="_i13"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(3)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq4"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_m004.gif" alt="" id="_i14"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(4)</span></div></div></span></div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/large/am-2018-01888n_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Kinetic analysis of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C: (a) CV curve at small scan rates (0.1, 0.3, 0.5, and 0.7 mV s<sup>–1</sup>), (b) CV curve at large scan rates (1.5, 3.0, 5.0, and 7.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>), (c) plots of <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> vs <i>I</i> used for calculating the diffusion coefficient, (d) liner of <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> vs <i>I</i>/<i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> for evaluating capacitive-controlled behaviors, (e) liner of log(<i>v</i>) vs log(<i>I</i>) obtained from the CV curve, (f) plots of log(<i>v</i>) vs log(<i>I</i>) at 0.1–7.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, (g) ratio of pseudo-capacitive capacity at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, and (h) contribution ratio of capacitive vs diffusion at a stepwise scan rate.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/large/am-2018-01888n_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b01888&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="eq 1">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq1" aria-label="1">1</a>, <i>n</i> is the transform electrons in the reaction, <i>A</i> is the area contracting with the electrolyte, <i>D</i> is the diffusion coefficient, <i>C</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> is about the concentration of sodium ions, and <i>v</i> and <i>I</i><sub>p</sub> are the scan rate and the relative peak current, respectively. <i>I</i><sub>p</sub>/<i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> can be fitted to 2.19 and −1.31 for oxidation and reduction peaks, and the corresponding <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> is calculated to be 1.03 × 10<sup>–12</sup> and 0.37 × 10<sup>–12</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. The average diffusion coefficient can reach to 0.7 × 10<sup>–12</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, revealing the fast ion shuttling.</div><div class="NLM_p">Benefitting from the Dunn’s work, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50 ref51 ref54" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref50 ref51 ref54" aria-label="reference 50, 51 and 54">(50,51,54)</a> the energy storage types were clear, containing Faradaic process (pesudocapacitive behaviors and diffusion-controlled behaviors) and non-Faradaic process (electric double layer). <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq3" aria-label="Equation 3">Equation </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq3" aria-label="3">3</a> comes from <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq2" aria-label="eq 2">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq2" aria-label="2">2</a>, and when b is close to 1, indicating the capacitive-controlled behaviors, and b approaches to 0.5, suggesting the diffusion-controlled behaviors. Clearly, in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>e, the <i>b</i> value of Peak 1 ≈ Peak 4 is 0.82, 0.78, 0.80, and 0.79, which demonstrate that the electrochemical properties for CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C were dominated by the pesudocapacitive behaviors. When the scan rate increased to 7.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, it is found that the slope of Peak 1 stabilizes 0.80 in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>f. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>c, the well liner relationship between <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> and <i>I</i>/<i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> is observed and the slope <i>k</i><sub>1</sub> and intercept <i>k</i><sub>2</sub> can be obtained for calculating the ratio of capacitive behaviors. On the basis of <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq4" aria-label="eq 4">eq </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq4" aria-label="4">4</a>, <i>k</i><sub>1</sub><i>v</i> is in relation with the capacitive-controlled contributions and <i>k</i><sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> is associated with the insertion behavior. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>g displays the detail-fitting curve for pseudocapacitive contribution at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, agreeing well with the previous report. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> Taking increased scan rates into consideration, the capacitive contributions are rising, about 67% at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, 75% at 0.3 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, 80% at 0.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, 81% at 0.7 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, 92% at 1.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, 94% at 3.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, 95% at 5.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, and 96% at 7.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. These enhanced capacitive behaviors disclosed that the capacitive behaviors contribute to the major capacity at large current density, perhaps derived from the significant merits of the structure.</div><div class="NLM_p">The EIS was conducted to analyze the internal impedance, and in situ EIS was performed to investigate the phase transform accompanying with slight variation of resistance. The Nyquist plots at undischarged condition and the relative fitting liner are shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a, and the relative equivalent circuit was exhibited in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>b. The curves can be divided into two parts: (1) the semicircle in high frequency is about <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> (the resistance of materials in the cell, containing electrode, electrolyte, and separation), <i>R</i><sub>f</sub> (the impedance of SEI films), and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (the resistance of charge transfer) and (2) the line in low frequency is about <i>Z</i><sub>W</sub> (Warburg impedance and the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in the target sample). Obviously, the small <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C is 39 Ω, which is due to the high conductivity of the as-obtained sample. After various cycles (10th, 30th, 60th, 100th, and 200th), it is found that <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> almost remains unchanged at 34 Ω, revealing a stable electrochemical reaction. According to <a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq5" aria-label="eqs 5">eqs </a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq5" aria-label="5">5</a>–<a class="ref internalNav" href="#eq7" aria-label="7">7</a> as following, the diffusion coefficient from the line in the low frequency could be obtained. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref55 ref56" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref55 ref56" aria-label="reference 55 and 56">(55,56)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq5"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_m005.gif" alt="" id="_i15"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(5)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq6"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_m006.gif" alt="" id="_i16"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(6)</span></div></div></span><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="eq7"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_m007.gif" alt="" id="_i17"></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(7)</span></div></div></span></div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/large/am-2018-01888n_0007.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. Electrochemical impedance analysis of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C: (a) Nyquist plots at undischarged condition, (b) corresponding equivalent circuit, (c) Nyquist plots after different cyclings, (d) plots of <i>w</i><sup>1/2</sup> vs −<i>Z</i>″, (e) in situ Nyquist plots at different discharge conditions and (f) at different charge conditions, and (g) various platform vs phase transforms.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/large/am-2018-01888n_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b01888&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Fitting <i>Z</i><sub>re</sub> and ω<sup>–1/2</sup> is to gain the Warburg factor σ about 51, 47, 45, and 43 at 10th, 30th, 60th, and 100th cycles, respectively, which is used for calculating that their <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> are 5.3 × 10<sup>–14</sup>, 6.3 × 10<sup>–14</sup>, 6.8 × 10<sup>–14</sup>, and 7.4 × 10<sup>–14</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, respectively. The <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> differed from the analysis, which is ascribed to the different calculating models. With the proceeding cycling, their <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> values were increasing, which is ascribed to the slight residual Co from the incomplete reconversion reaction in the electrode. In situ EIS was carried out to evaluate the reaction process at 500th cycle, as displayed in <a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>. When discharged, at 2.5 V, no sodium ions inserted into the samples. Decreasing the voltage decreases the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>, which is attributed to that the pure Co and Na<sub>2</sub>Se could provide effective with matrix high conductivity, facilitating ion transfer. When charged, the resistance is increasing and returned to the pristine resistance, suggesting the high reversible and outstanding kinetics. The analysis of EIS demonstrated that the small resistance of the target product acts an important role in the electrochemical reaction.</div><div class="NLM_p">In the sodiation/desodiation process, the stable crystalline structure and morphology are of importance for the electrode. The explorations of the CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C electrode after 500 loops were probed through ex situ technologies. In <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>a, with the comparison of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C after three cycles at 1.5 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, the peaks of CV curves after 500 cycles become sharper, indicating that the phase transition occurred in a narrow potential, which is beneficial for the jarless electrochemical properties. In <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/suppl_file/am8b01888_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S4</a>, the CV curves from 501th to 508th were displayed; it is found that their shape remain same, indicating the stable electrochemical reaction. Furthermore, their XRD pattern coincides well with the pristine one, demonstrating their stable crystal structure, but the intensity of peaks is weaker, revealing the lowered crystalline. According to the discussion about <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a, the peaks moving toward high angles and the lowered full wave at half maximum demonstrate the deducing particles. In the Raman spectra, the peak intensity of poly(vinylidene difluoride) is almost similar, and that of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C is weaken, which may be due to the lowered crystalline, the formation of SEI film, and the reduction of particles. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> This is consistent with the analysis of ex situ XRD. Clearly, with the protection of the carbon matrix, the shape of CoSe<sub>2</sub> nanospheres remains unchanged after 500 cycles in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>d,e. Note that the morphology of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C has some change but still has a similar sphere structure and placed in the carbon matrix; meanwhile, slight Co grains were produced in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>g. The spacing lattice of CoSe<sub>2</sub> is found to remain stable. Moreover, the lattice distance (0.193 nm) is indexed to the (111) facet of standard Co (JCPDs card: 88-2325). In the illustration of <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig8" id="" class=" internalNav">8</a>g, the diffraction rings are indexed to (200), (211), and (311) planes of standard CoSe<sub>2</sub> (JCPDs: 88-1712) and (111) facets of Co. It can be concluded that the target sample display excellent stability of structure and morphology.</div><figure id="fig8" data-index="8" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 8</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/medium/am-2018-01888n_0008.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/large/am-2018-01888n_0008.jpeg" id="gr8" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 8. Ex situ exploration of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C electrode 500 loops: (a) CV curves, (b) XRD patterns, (c) Raman spectra, (d,e) SEM images at charged 3.0 V, and (f,g) TEM images at charged 3.0 V.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/asset/images/large/am-2018-01888n_0008.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.8b01888&amp;id=fig8"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i18">4.  Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, the effective 3D hierarchical selenium cobalt framework assembled by 0D CoSe<sub>2</sub>@C cobblestone-like nanospheres was obtained through significant mixing and sintering. The citric acid supplies plentiful oxygen-containing functional groups, inducing the formation of uniform carbon matrix and Co–O–C bonds, thereby imparting improvement on the electrochemical properties. Utilizing the adaptive electrolyte (NaCF<sub>3</sub>SO<sub>3</sub>/DEGDME), the ultralong lifespan was shown at a large current density of 4.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> between 0.5 and 3.0 V, delivering a capacity of 345 mA h g<sup>–1</sup> after 10 000 cycles. In spite of upgrading potential platform, the excellent cycling stability is of important for the commercial application. Ex situ characterization demonstrated the stable crystal structure and morphological texture after the fast sodiation/desodiation process. In addition, the detailed kinetic analysis for CV and in situ EIS further reveal the ion transferring process and conversion mechanism. It is anticipated that this paper can enhance the in-depth understanding of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C with Co–O–C bonds and provide significant manner to obtain CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C as anodes for SIBs.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>45</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1308</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1330</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c5cs00708a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D45%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D1308-1330%26journal%3DChem.%2BSoc.%2BRev.%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BChen%26author%3DO.%2BG.%2BSchmidt%26author%3DC.%2BYan%26title%3DEngineered%2Bnanomembranes%2Bfor%2Bsmart%2Benergy%2Bstorage%2Bdevices%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc5cs00708a&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b01888&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc5cs00708a&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineered nanomembranes for smart energy storage devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xianfu; Chen, Yu; Schmidt, Oliver G.; Yan, Chenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">45</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1308-1330</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineered nanomembranes are of great interest not only for large-scale energy storage devices, but also for on-chip energy storage integrated microdevices (such as microbatteries, microsupercapacitors, on-chip capacitors, etc.) because of their large active surfaces for electrochem. reactions, shortened paths for fast ion diffusion, and easy engineering for microdevice applications.  In addn., engineered nanomembranes provide a lab-on-chip electrochem. device platform for probing the correlations of electrode structure, elec./ionic cond., and electrochem. kinetics with device performance.  This review focuses on the recent progress in engineered nanomembranes including tubular nanomembranes and planar nanomembranes, with the aim to provide a systematic summary of their fabrication, modification, and energy storage applications in lithium-ion batteries, lithium-oxygen batteries, on-chip electrostatic capacitors and micro-supercapacitors.  A comprehensive understanding of the relationship between engineered nanomembranes and electrochem. properties of lithium ion storage with engineered single-tube microbatteries is given, and the flexibility and transparency of micro-supercapacitors is also discussed.  Remarks on challenges and perspectives related to engineered nanomembranes for the further development of energy storage applications conclude this review.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref2" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c4cs00218k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured Mn-based oxides for electrochemical energy storage and conversion</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>44</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">699</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">728</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c4cs00218k</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D44%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D699-728%26journal%3DChem.%2BSoc.%2BRev.%26author%3DK.%2BZhang%26author%3DX.%2BHan%26author%3DZ.%2BHu%26author%3DX.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BTao%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DNanostructured%2BMn-based%2Boxides%2Bfor%2Belectrochemical%2Benergy%2Bstorage%2Band%2Bconversion%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc4cs00218k&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b01888&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc4cs00218k&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured Mn-based oxides for electrochemical energy storage and conversion</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Han, Xiaopeng; Hu, Zhe; Zhang, Xiaolong; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">699-728</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Batteries and supercapacitors as electrochem. energy storage and conversion devices are continuously serving for human life.  The electrochem. performance of batteries and supercapacitors depends in large part on the active materials in electrodes.  As an important family, Mn-based oxides have shown versatile applications in primary batteries, secondary batteries, metal-air batteries, and pseudocapacitors due to their high activity, high abundance, low price, and environmental friendliness.  In order to meet future market demand, it is essential and urgent to make further improvements in energy and power densities of Mn-based electrode materials with the consideration of multiple electron reaction and low mol. wt. of the active materials.  Meanwhile, nanomaterials are favorable to achieve high performance by means of shortening the ionic diffusion length and providing large surface areas for electrode reactions.  This article reviews the recent efforts made to apply nanostructured Mn-based oxides for batteries and pseudocapacitors.  The influence of structure, morphol., and compn. on electrochem. performance has been systematically summarized.  Compared to bulk materials and notable metal catalysts, nanostructured Mn-based oxides can promote the thermodn. and kinetics of the electrochem. reactions occurring at the solid-liq. or the solid-liq.-gas interface.  In particular, nanostructured Mn-based oxides such as one-dimensional MnO2 nanostructures, MnO2-conductive matrix nanocomposites, concn.-gradient structured layered Li-rich Mn-based oxides, porous LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 nanorods, core-shell structured LiMnSiO4@C nanocomposites, spinel-type Co-Mn-O nanoparticles, and perovskite-type CaMnO3 with micro-nano structures all display superior electrochem. performance.  This review should shed light on the sustainable development of advanced batteries and pseudocapacitors with nanostructured Mn-based oxides.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref3" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201090116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cabana, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monconduit, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Larcher, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacin, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">This review highlights the recent developments and the future prospects of the use of phases that react through conversion reactions as both cathode and anode materials in Li-ion batteries.  By moving beyond classical intercalation reactions, a variety of low cost compds. with gravimetric specific capacities that are 2-5 times larger than those attained with currently used materials, such as graphite and LiCoO2, can be achieved.  Nonetheless, several factors currently handicap the applicability of electrode materials entailing conversion reactions.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Large-area phosphorus-doped carbon nanosheets (P-CNSs) are first obtained from carbon dots (CDs) through self-assembly driving from thermal treatment with Na catalysis.  This is the first time to realize the conversion from 0D CDs to 2D nanosheets doped with phosphorus.  The sodium storage behavior of phosphorus-doped carbon material is also investigated for the first time.  As anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), P-CNSs exhibit superb performances for electrochemical storage of sodium.  When cycled at 0.1 A g(-1), the P-CNSs electrode delivers a high reversible capacity of 328 mAh g(-1), even at a high current density of 20 A g(-1), a considerable capacity of 108 mAh g(-1) can still be maintained.         </div><div class="casAbstract">We report a Se composite cathode material, in which Se is confined as a cyclic Se8 mols. in the mesopores of an ordered mesoporous carbon (CMK-3) matrix.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  To meet the increasing demand for electrochem. energy storage with high energy d., elemental Se is proposed as a new attractive candidate with high volumetric capacity d. similar to that of S.  Se is chem. and electrochem. analogous to S to a large extent but is saliently featured owing to its semicond., compatibility with carbonate-based electrolytes, and activity with a Na anode.  Despite only short-term studies, many advanced Se-based electrode materials have been developed for rechargeable Li batteries, Na batteries, and Li ion batteries.  In this Perspective, the authors review the advances in Se-based energy storage materials and the challenges of Li-Se battery in both carbonate-based and ether-based electrolytes.  The authors also discuss the rational design strategies for future Se-based energy storage systems based on the strengths and weaknesses of Se.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref12" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b16708"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, W.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xin, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ye, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, Y.-X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphitic Nanocarbon-Selenium Cathode with Favorable Rate Capability for Li-Se Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Substitution of selenium for sulfur in the cathode of a rechargeable battery contg. Sx mols. in microporous slits in carbon allows a better characterization of the electrochem. reactions that occur.  Paired with a metallic lithium anode, the Sex chains are converted to Li2Se in a single-step reaction.  With a sodium anode, a sequential chem. reaction is characterized by a continuous chain shortening of Sex upon initial discharge before completing the redn. to Na2Se; on charge, the reconstituted Sex mols. retain a smaller x value than the original Sex chain mol.  In both cases, the Se mols. remain almost completely confined to the micropore slits to give a long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.01.097"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">In situ X-ray diffraction characterization of NiSe<sub>2</sub> as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ X-ray diffraction characterization of NiSe2 as a promising anode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Xing; Li, Jiao; Zheng, Fenghua; Wu, Peng; Pan, Qichang; Xiong, Xunhui; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Reduced graphene oxide (rGO) homogenously wrapped nickel diselenide (NiSe2/rGO) hybrid was prepd. by a facile one-spot hydrothermal method.  When investigated as anode material for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), NiSe2/rGO hybrid delivers a high reversible capacity (433 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1), superior rate performance (406, 386, 366, 347 and 318 mAh g-1 at 200, 500, 1000, 2000 and 5000 mA g-1, resp.) and excellent cycling stability (a capacity retention of 346 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at 1000 mA g-1) within the 0.4-3.0 V voltage range.  In situ x-ray diffraction anal. and ex situ SEM/TEM measurement reveal that the high capacity of NiSe2/rGO is originated from the combined Na+ intercalation and conversion reactions.  These results validate the impact of voltage range on electrochem. property, providing a new route to rationalize the limiting factors that affect the performance of NiSe2 anode material.  The facile synthesis and superior electrochem. performance of the NiSe2/rGO hybrid render it a promising anode material for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201500196"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">FeSe2 Microspheres as a High-Performance Anode Material for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. The FeSe2 microspheres assembled by nanooctahedra display a high tapping d. of 1.85 g cm-3 and a discharge capacity of 447 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.  The FeSe2 anode also exhibits long-term cyclic stability (372 mA h g-1 with capacity retention of 89.0% after 2000 cycles at 1 A g-1 ) and excellent high-rate performance 388 mA h g-1 at 10 C, 337 mA h g-1 at 20 C, 226 mA h g-1 at 50 C, where 1 C = 0.5 A g-1.  The conversion reaction of FeSe2 + 4Na+ + 4e ↔ Fe + 2Na2Se has been confirmed.  Furthermore, the FeSe2 anode is coupled with an excessive Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode (the capacity of the Na3V2(PO4)3 is 1.5-2 times more than that of FeSe2) to fabricate a full cell, which exhibits a discharge capacity of 366 mA h g-1 based on the mass of FeSe2 with an av. output voltage of about 1.7 V at 1 A g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b10143"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">NiSe2 Nanooctahedra as an Anode Material for High-Rate and Long-Life Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this article, we report NiSe2 nanooctahedra as a promising anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  They exhibit outstanding long-term cyclic stability (313 mAh/g after 4000 cycles at 5 A/g) and excellent high-rate capability (175 mAh/g at 20 A/g).  Besides, the initial Coulombic efficiency of NiSe2 is also very impressive (over 90%).  Such remarkable performances are attributed to good cond., structural stability, and the pseudocapacitive behavior of the NiSe2.  Furthermore, the sodium ion storage mechanism of NiSe2 is first investigated by in situ XRD and ex situ XRD.  These highlights give NiSe2 a competitive strength for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201602608"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, G.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Urchin-Like CoSe2 as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tuning the Electronic Bandgap: An Efficient Way To Improve the Electrocatalytic Activity of Carbon-Supported Co3O4 Nanocrystals for Oxygen Reduction Reactions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Hongcan; Long, Wujie; Song, Weiwei; Liu, Jingjun; Wang, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

Herein, the authors prepd. spherical Co3O4 nanoparticles with a preferred orientation along the (111) plane by direct nucleation and growth of the oxide on graphitized C black (GCB). Electrocatalysis expts. in an alk. environment revealed that the electrocatalytic activity for ORR on the preferred (111) oxide increased as a function of the degree of crystal-lattice orientation, which implies a closely intrinsic correlation between the predominant (111) plane and the catalytic activity.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional stable metallic 1T-MoSe2 with expanded interlayer spacing of 10.0 Å in situ grown on SWCNTs film is fabricated via a one-step solvothermal method.  Combined with X-ray absorption near-edge structures, our characterization reveals that such 1T-MoSe2 and single-walled carbon nanotubes (abbreviated as 1T-MoSe2/SWCNTs) hybridized structure can provide strong elec. and chem. coupling between 1T-MoSe2 nanosheets and SWCNT film in a form of C-O-Mo bonding, which significantly benefits a high-efficiency electron/ion transport pathway and structural stability, thus directly enabling high-performance lithium storage properties.  In particular, as a flexible and binder-free Li-ion anode, the 1T-MoSe2/SWCNTs electrode exhibits excellent rate capacity, which delivers a capacity of 630 mAh/g at 3000 mA/g.  Meanwhile, the strong C-O-Mo bonding of 1T-MoSe2/SWCNTs accommodates vol. alteration during the repeated charge/discharge process, which gives rise to 89% capacity retention and a capacity of 971 mAh/g at 300 mA/g after 100 cycles.  This synthetic route of a multifunctional MoSe2/SWCNTs hybrid might be extended to fabricate other 2D layer-based flexible and light electrodes for various applications such as electronics, optics, and catalysts.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.09.032"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The electrochemical exploration of double carbon-wrapped Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> : Towards long-time cycling and superior rate sodium-ion battery cathode</span>. <i>J. The p-CoSe2 is obtained by calcining CoSex via electrodeposition at 300°.  The results of X-ray diffraction (XRD) and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) demonstrated the crystal structure of p-CoSe2.  The p-CoSe2 exhibits excellent electrocatalytic activity for HER with a low onset overpotential of -70 mV and a small Tafel slope of ∼30 mV/decade, which are basically state-of-the-art performance of earth-abundant electrocatalysts.  The HER performance of p-CoSe2 was much higher than that of amorphous CoSex, cubic CoSe2, and CoSe.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nano-crystals of cerium-hafnium binary oxide: Their size-dependent structure</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Raitano, Joan M.; Khalid, Syed; Marinkovic, Nebojsa; Chan, Siu-Wai</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">644</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">996-1002</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Cerium oxide (CeO2, "ceria") and hafnium oxide (HfO2, "hafnia") were aqueously co-pptd. and subsequently calcined to allow for homogenization.  The size of the (1-x)CeO2-xHfO2 crystallites, detd. by the Scherrer equation, varied from 140 nm for x = 0 to 15 nm for x = 0.73.  For x ≤ 0.14, only cubic structures are visible in X-ray diffractograms, and the lattice parameters are consistent with the values expected for structurally cubic solid solns. of hafnia in ceria.  At x = 0.26, tetragonal and monoclinic phases nucleated with the former not being obsd. in the bulk phase diagram for ceria-hafnia.  Therefore, the soly. limit of the cubic structure is between x = 0.14 and x = 0.26 for 40-61 nm crystallites, the sizes of these resp. compns.  More specifically, for the 40 nm crystallites of x = 0.26 (1-x)CeO2-xHfO2, 15% of the hafnia remains in a structurally cubic solid soln. with ceria based on the obsd. cubic lattice parameter.  The compositional domain for the cubic fluorite structure in this study is narrower than other nanostructured (1-x)CeO2-xHfO2 studies, esp. studies with crystallite sizes &lt;10 nm, but wider than obsd. in the bulk and helps to expand the size regime over which the relationship between crystallite size and phase stability is known. The RGO anode allowed significant Na ion insertion, leading to higher capacity at high c.d. compared to the previously reported results for C materials.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanostructured CoSe2 anode materials hold great promise for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), drawing much recent research attention.  However, high-performance CoSe2 based anodes are still challenging to obtain.  Herein, using zeolitic imidazolate framework-67 (ZIF-67) particles as the starting material, nondestructive hollow polyhedral hybrids were synthesized successfully, which are structured from CNT-bridged carbon-coated CoSe2 nanospheres (CoSe2@C/CNTs).  During the synthesis, the controlled in situ growth of CNTs introduces addnl. mesopores and open channels to the hybrids, and avoids serious agglomeration of the CoSe2 nanospheres.  When employed as anode materials for SIBs with ether-based electrolyte, the CoSe2@C/CNTs show overwhelming merits over graphitic carbon-coated CoSe2 nanosphere polyhedral hybrids (CoSe2@GC) and bare CoSe2 particles.  Specifically, the CoSe2@C/CNTs anode displays a high reversible capacity (∼470 mA h g-1 at 0.2 A g-1), a good rate capability of ∼373 mA h g-1 even at 10 A g-1, and an excellent cycling stability of over 1000 cycles with a capacity retention of ∼100% calcd. from the 70th cycle.  In addn., the electrochem. reaction dynamics anal. indicates a considerable capacitive contribution during the discharge-charge cycles, which is beneficial to enhance the rate capability and cyclability of the CoSe2@C/CNTs anode.  Such results could be ascribed to the stable ether-based electrolyte-active material intermediates, improved electrolyte-active material contact, and shortened charge transfer paths afforded by the unique hybrid nanostructure.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1039/c4cy00017j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huo, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Core-shell structured Fe3O4@SiO2 supported cobalt(II) or copper(II) acetylacetonate complexes: magnetically recoverable nanocatalysts for aerobic epoxidation of styrene</span>. <i>Catal.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Org.-inorg. hybrid heterogeneous nanocatalysts were successfully fabricated via covalent anchoring of cobalt(II) or copper(II) acetylacetonate complexes ([Co(acac)2] or [Cu(acac)2]) onto core-shell structured Fe3O4@SiO2 previously functionalized with 3-aminopropyltriethoxysilane (APTES).                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mn3O4-decorated Co3O4 nanoparticles supported on graphene oxide: Dual electrocatalyst system for oxygen reduction reaction in alkaline medium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dai, Lijun; Liu, Min; Song, Ye; Liu, Jingjun; Wang, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing composite materials with a smart nanostructure, by using various transition metal oxides and carbon carriers as building blocks, is of great importance to develop highly active, economical noble metal-free catalysts for oxygen redn. reaction (ORR).  We have synthesized a novel ternary composite with a special 3D stacked-up nanostructure, composed of Co3O4, Mn3O4 and graphene oxide (GO), via a facile two-step aq. synthesis without adding any structure directing agent.  The composite was characterized by X-ray diffraction, scanning transmission electron microscope, Raman spectroscopy, and XPS.  The results revealed that Mn3O4 nanocrystals had been successfully epitaxially deposited onto the surface of Co3O4 nanoparticles to form Mn3O4-on-Co3O4 nanostructures on surface of the graphene.  In an alk. environment, the Co3O4-Mn3O4/GO composite exhibits much better electrocatalytic activity and durability towards ORR than individual Mn3O4/GO and Co3O4/GO catalysts.  The recorded kinetic c.d. (JK) of O2 redn. for the composite is 2.078 mA/cm2, which is comparable to that of a com. Pt/C (20%) but far exceeding the sum of that obtained from the Co3O4/GO and Mn3O4/GO.  The remarkably improved ORR activity is closely attributed to the enhanced synergy between these two oxides and the graphene, raised by the 3D stacked-up structure in this composite.  The oxide-on-oxide heterostructure comprising Co3O4 and Mn3O4 can promote covalent electron transfer from carbon support to the oxides as a result of the interphase ligand effect between them, which facilitate the ORR kinetics.  Moreover, Mn3O4 phase acting as a co-catalyst, located at the top of Co3O4 phase, also favor the chem. disproportionation of H2O2 intermediates generated by the composite during the ORR.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.jallcom.2017.10.094"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Co 0.85 Se nanosheets/graphene composite film as binder-free anode with high Li- and Na-Ion storage performance</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Co0.85Se nanosheets/graphene composite film as binder-free anode with high Li- and Na-Ion storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Guanjun; Liu, Kunhong; Liu, Sitong; Song, Huaihe; Zhou, Jisheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">731</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">714-722</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A free-standing Co0.85Se nanosheets/graphene (Co0.85Se NSs/G) composite film was developed as a high performance anode material for both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) by a simple vacuum filtration and thermal redn. process.  The Co0.85Se NSs/G film demonstrates good flexibility, and the Co0.85Se NSs are uniformly anchored on the graphene to form "sheet-on-sheet" nanostructures with strong interfacial interactions.  The hybrid lamellar film demonstrated excellent electrochem. performances when used as a binder-free anode for LIBs and SIBs.  As an anode material for LIBs, the Co0.85Se NSs/G film exhibited a high initial reversible capacity of 680 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and an excellent cycling stability and rate performance.  The specific capacity of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film shows almost no fading from 0.05 to 0.5 A g-1, and the capacities were maintained at 613.3 and 522.7 mA h g -1 at 1 and 2 A g-1, resp.  When used as an anode for SIBs, the reversible capacity of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film reached up to 388 mA h g-1 with an initial coulombic efficiency as high as 82.5% at 50 mA g-1.  Even at the higher current densities of 1 and 2 A g-1, the reversible capacities remained at 137.5 and 112.4 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles, resp.  The excellent electrochem. performances should be attributed to the special structure of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film.  On one hand, graphene not only provides an efficient elec. conductive network, but also acts as an elastic layer to buffer the volumetric expansion of the Co0.85Se NSs during the discharge/charge process in LIBs/SIBs, which is helpful for enhancing the cycling stability of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film.  On the other hand, strong interfacial interactions can further enhance electron transfer between Co0.85Se NSs and graphene, which is beneficial for improving the cycling stability and rate-performance of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref37" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b13153"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pan, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-Doped Yolk-Shell-Structured CoSe/C Dodecahedra for High-Performance Sodium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ X-ray diffraction investigation of CoSe2 anode for Na-ion storage: Effect of cut-off voltage on cycling stability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Xing; Liang, Xinghui; Zheng, Fenghua; Wu, Peng; Pan, Qichang; Xiong, Xunhui; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">258</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1387-1396</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Owing to their high specific capacity, transition metal chalcogenides (TMCs) based materials attract enormous attentions for energy storage, yet the performance decay obsd. in TMCs anodes are strongly depended on the host material and working conditions.  Here the authors report CoSe2 nanorods as a promising alternative for Na-ion batteries (SIBs), which are fabricated by a facile hydrothermal strategy.  At upper cut-off voltage of 0.4 V, the as-prepd. sample can demonstrate improved sodiation capacity, rate capability, and cycling stability (a high capacity of 386 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 even after 2000 cycles).  In situ XRD and ex situ TEM measurements were used to study phase transition behavior of CoSe2 nanorods in the initial 9 sodiation/desodiation cycles.  The high electrochem. reversibility of CoSe2 nanorods within the potential window of 0.4-3.0 V is ascribed to that the deep conversion reaction &lt;0.4 V is effectively avoided, thus the vol. expansion and pulverization of CoSe2 nanorods are efficiently suppressed.  It convinces that applying suitable and optimal cut-off voltage is a useful approach to regulate the reactions progress for TMCs anode, improving their cycling and structure stability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201602608"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, G.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Urchin-Like CoSe<sub>2</sub> as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Urchin-Like CoSe2 as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Park, Mihui; Zhou, Limin; Lee, Gi-Hyeok; Li, Weijie; Kang, Yong-Mook; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Urchin-like CoSe2 assembled by nanorods was synthesized via simple solvothermal route and was 1st applied as an anode material for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) with ether-based electrolytes.  The CoSe2 delivers excellent sodiation and de-sodiation properties when using 1 M NaCF3SO3 in diethyleneglycol dimethylether as an electrolyte and cycling between 0.5 and 3.0 V.  A high discharge capacity of 0.410 A h g-1 is obtained at 1 A g-1 after 1800 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention of 98.6% calcd. from the 30th cycle.  Even at an ultrahigh rate of 50 A g-1, the capacity still maintains 0.097 A h g-1.  The reaction mechanism of the as-prepd. CoSe2 is also studied.  At discharged 1.56 V, insertion reaction occurs, while 2 conversion reactions take place at the 2nd and 3rd plateaus around 0.98 and 0.65 V.  During the charge process, Co 1st reacts with Na2Se to form NaxCoSe2 and then turns back to CoSe2.  In addn. to Na/CoSe2 half cells, Na3V2(PO4)3/CoSe2 full cell with excessive amt. of Na3V2(PO4)3 was studied.  The full cell exhibits a reversible capacity of 0.380 Ah g-1.  This work enriches the possibilities for anode materials for SIBs with high performance.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref42" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.07.079"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, S.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Excellent sodium-ion storage performances of CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded within N-doped porous graphitic carbon nanocube/carbon nanotube composite</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Park, Seung-Keun; Kim, Jin Koo; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A metal org. framework (MOF)-engaged approach is applied for the fabrication of CoSe2 nanoparticles embedded within N-doped porous graphitic C nanocubes/C nanotubes (CoSe2@N-PGC/CNTs).  The composites were prepd. by decompn. under the reducing atm. and further selenization of Co-based zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-67) precursor.  The metallic Co nanoparticles formed during the redn. process play a key role in catalyzing the in-situ formation of graphitic C and extrusion of CNTs from the surface of the composite nanocube using C sources originated from org. ligands in ZIF-67 templates.  The direct selenization process of ZIF-67 produces the composite nanocubes (CoSe2@AC) of CoSe2 and amorphous C.  The specific discharge capacities of the CoSe2@NPGC/CNTs and CoSe2@AC composite nanocubes after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1 were 424 and 100 mA h g-1, resp.  The excellent electrochem. performance of CoSe2@N-PGC/CNTs composite nanocubes are attributed to their unique compositional and structural features.                         cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Molybdenum Phosphide: A Conversion-type Anode for Ultralong-Life Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Zhaodong; Hou, Hongshuai; Wang, Chao; Li, Simin; Zhang, Yun; Ji, Xiaobo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

Herein, molybdenum phosphide (MoP) nanorods wrapped with thin carbon layer have been prepd. and applied as an anode for SIBs.  By utilizing in situ X-ray diffraction technol., a conversion-type mechanism of MoP anode has been disclosed.  This kind of MoP electrode exhibits extraordinary electrochem. properties, including excellent cycling performance with a discharge capacity of 398.4 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1 after 800 cycles, and remarkable rate capabilities, which remain 104.5 mA g-1 at 1600 mA h g-1 even after 10,000 loops.  The distinguished performances stem from synergetic merits of the morphol., structure, and mechanism of MoP.  It is expected that MoP will be a promising anode material for SIBs and this work would provide theor. basis for the scalable research and applications of MoP-based anode materials for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201602880"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrafine MoO<sub>2</sub>-Carbon Microstructures Enable Ultralong-Life Power-Type Sodium Ion Storage by Enhanced Pseudocapacitance</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ordered mesoporous α-MoO3 with iso-oriented nanocrystalline walls for thin-film pseudocapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brezesinski, Torsten; Wang, John; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">146-151</span>CODEN:
