            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Capacitive energy storage is distinguished from other types of electrochem. energy storage by short charging times and the ability to deliver significantly more power than batteries.  A limitation to this technol. is its low energy d. and there is interest in exploring pseudo-capacitive materials where faradaic mechanisms offer increased energy storage.  The capacitive charge-storage properties of mesoporous films of iso-oriented α-MoO3 are superior to those of either mesoporous amorphous material or nonporous cryst. MoO3.  Whereas both cryst. and amorphous mesoporous materials show redox pseudo-capacitance, the iso-oriented layered cryst. domains enable Li ions to be inserted into the van der Waals gaps of the α-MoO3.  Probably this extra contribution arises from an intercalation pseudo-capacitance, which occurs on the same timescale as redox pseudo-capacitance.  The result is increased charge-storage capacity without compromising charge/discharge kinetics in mesoporous cryst. MoO3.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref52" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms7929"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation pseudocapacitance in graphene-coupled titanium oxide enabling ultra-fast sodium storage and long-term cycling</span>. <i>Nat. Commun.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>6</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6929</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1038/ncomms7929</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D6929%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26author%3DC.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BWen%26author%3DX.%2BHu%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26author%3DM.%2BYan%26author%3DL.%2BMai%26author%3DP.%2BHu%26author%3DB.%2BShan%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26title%3DNa%252B%2Bintercalation%2Bpseudocapacitance%2Bin%2Bgraphene-coupled%2Btitanium%2Boxide%2Benabling%2Bultra-fast%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%2Band%2Blong-term%2Bcycling%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms7929&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b01888&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms7929&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in graphene-coupled titanium oxide enabling ultra-fast sodium storage and long-term cycling</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chaoji; Wen, Yanwei; Hu, Xianluo; Ji, Xiulei; Yan, Mengyu; Mai, Liqiang; Hu, Pei; Shan, Bin; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6929</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are emerging as a highly promising technol. for large-scale energy storage applications.  However, it remains a significant challenge to develop an anode with superior long-term cycling stability and high-rate capability.  Here we demonstrate that the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitance in TiO2/graphene nanocomposites enables high-rate capability and long cycle life in a sodium-ion battery.  This hybrid electrode exhibits a specific capacity of above 90 mA h g-1 at 12,000 mA g-1 (∼36 C).  The capacity is highly reversible for more than 4,000 cycles, the longest demonstrated cyclability to date.  First-principle calcns. demonstrate that the intimate integration of graphene with TiO2 reduces the diffusion energy barrier, thus enhancing the Na+ intercalation pseudocapacitive process.  The Na-ion intercalation pseudocapacitance enabled by tailor-deigned nanostructures represents a promising strategy for developing electrode materials with high power d. and long cycle life.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref53" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1016/j.matchemphys.2017.10.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Enhanced stability of sodium storage exhibited by carbon coated Sb<sub>2</sub>S<sub>3</sub> hollow spheres</span>. <i>Mater. Chem. Phys.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>203</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">185</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">192</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.matchemphys.2017.10.003</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D203%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D185-192%26journal%3DMater.%2BChem.%2BPhys.%26author%3DP.%2BGe%26author%3DH.%2BHou%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26author%3DZ.%2BHuang%26author%3DS.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BHuang%26title%3DEnhanced%2Bstability%2Bof%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%2Bexhibited%2Bby%2Bcarbon%2Bcoated%2BSb2S3%2Bhollow%2Bspheres%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.matchemphys.2017.10.003&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b01888&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.matchemphys.2017.10.003&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced stability of sodium storage exhibited by carbon coated Sb2S3 hollow spheres</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ge, Peng; Hou, Hongshuai; Ji, Xiaobo; Huang, Zhaodong; Li, Simin; Huang, Lanping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Chemistry and Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">203</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">185-192</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MCHPDR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0254-0584</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony sulfide (Sb2S3) has been shown as a promising candidate for sodium ions batteries, in considering the gravimetric energy d. and high theor. capacity.  Hollow-sphere Sb2S3 coated with carbon are successfully designed through Oswald ripening process.  The Sb2S3/C utilized as SIBs anode displays excellent electrochem. properties, delivering a high charge capacity of 693.4 mAh g-1 at 0.2 A g-1 between 0.01 and 3.0 V (vs. Na+/Na).  Its reversible capacity can keep 545.6 mAh g-1, with a retention of ∼80% after 100 cycles.  Even the current densities return from 6.4 to 0.2 A g-1, the Sb2S3/C still maintains 550.8 mAh g-1 after 70 cycles.  Combining the large void space with carbon layer, the advantages are noticed when the increased electrolyte penetration area, improved electronic cond. and shortened Na+ diffusion length are attained concurrently, resulting in the excellent specific capacity and cycling stability.  The study provides an effect strategy in improving the electrochem. performances of metal sulfides as anode for SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref54" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1021/jp074464w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Polleux, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dunn, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitive contributions to electrochemical energy storage in TiO<sub>2</sub> (anatase) nanoparticles</span>. <i>J. Phys. Chem. C</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2007</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>111</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14925</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14931</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jp074464w</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D111%26publication_year%3D2007%26pages%3D14925-14931%26journal%3DJ.%2BPhys.%2BChem.%2BC%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BPolleux%26author%3DJ.%2BLim%26author%3DB.%2BDunn%26title%3DPseudocapacitive%2Bcontributions%2Bto%2Belectrochemical%2Benergy%2Bstorage%2Bin%2BTiO2%2B%2528anatase%2529%2Bnanoparticles%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fjp074464w&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b01888&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fjp074464w&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pseudocapacitive Contributions to Electrochemical Energy Storage in TiO2 (Anatase) Nanoparticles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, John; Polleux, Julien; Lim, James; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2007</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">111</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">40</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14925-14931</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages of using nanostructured materials for electrochem. energy storage have focused on the benefits assocd. with short path lengths.  However, another contribution, capacitive effects which become increasingly important at nanoscale dimensions, was studied.  Nanocryst. TiO2 (anatase) was studied over a dimensional regime where both capacitive and Li intercalation processes contribute to the total stored charge.  An anal. of the voltammetric sweep data was used to distinguish between the amt. of charge stored by these 2 processes.  At particle sizes &lt;10 nm, capacitive contributions became increasingly important, leading to greater amts. of total stored charge (gravimetrically normalized) with decreasing TiO2 particle size.  The area normalized capacitance is well &gt;100 μF/cm2, confirming that the capacitive contribution was pseudocapacitive.  Also, decreasing the particle size to the nanoscale regime led to faster charge/discharge rates because diffusion-controlled Li ion intercalation was replaced by faradaic reactions which occur at the surface of the material.  The charge storage and kinetic benefits derived from using nanoscale metal oxides provide an interesting direction for the design of materials that offer both power d. and energy d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref55" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.02.086"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prabakar, S.
J. R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pyo, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanoporous hard carbon anodes for improved electrochemical performance in sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>161</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">23</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">31</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.02.086</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D161%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D23-31%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DS.%250AJ.%2BR.%2BPrabakar%26author%3DJ.%2BJeong%26author%3DM.%2BPyo%26title%3DNanoporous%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bimproved%2Belectrochemical%2Bperformance%2Bin%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2015.02.086&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b01888&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2015.02.086&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoporous hard carbon anodes for improved electrochemical performance in sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Prabakar, S. J. Richard; Jeong, Jaehyang; Pyo, Myoungho</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">161</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23-31</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The porosity and morphol. of sucrose-based hard carbon (SHC) was regulated by varying the amt. of bicarbonate salts added during a simple two-stage sintering process.  During the first-stage thermal treatment of sugar at 200°, CO2 liberated from bicarbonate contributed to the pulverization of particles and to the formation of submicron-sized pores.  Na2CO3 entrapped in a precursor matrix also released CO2 during the second-stage sintering at 850°, producing nanometric pores (∼10 nm in diam.).  The excessively high content of bicarbonates, however, resulted in paper-thin graphitic layers with no submicron-sized pores.  These dual roles of bicarbonates produced nanoporous SHC (NSHC) with the submicron-to-nano-sized pores and the largest surface area that was possible for a specific bicarbonate concn.  The optimal nanoporosity of NSHC lent itself to a sharp increase in reversible capacity.  Reversible capacity of 324 and 289 mA h g-1 were obtained for the first and 100th cycles at 20 mA g-1, in contrast to 251 and 213 mA h g-1, resp., for SHC.  The rate capability of NSHC also was enhanced due to a substantial decrease in the charge transfer resistance and a 5-fold increase in the Na+ diffusion coeff.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201800080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multidimensional Evolution of Carbon Structures Underpinned by Temperature-Induced Intermediate of Chloride for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineered nanomembranes for smart energy storage devices</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>45</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1308</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1330</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c5cs00708a</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Engineered nanomembranes for smart energy storage devices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xianfu; Chen, Yu; Schmidt, Oliver G.; Yan, Chenglin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">45</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1308-1330</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Engineered nanomembranes are of great interest not only for large-scale energy storage devices, but also for on-chip energy storage integrated microdevices (such as microbatteries, microsupercapacitors, on-chip capacitors, etc.) because of their large active surfaces for electrochem. reactions, shortened paths for fast ion diffusion, and easy engineering for microdevice applications.  In addn., engineered nanomembranes provide a lab-on-chip electrochem. device platform for probing the correlations of electrode structure, elec./ionic cond., and electrochem. kinetics with device performance.  This review focuses on the recent progress in engineered nanomembranes including tubular nanomembranes and planar nanomembranes, with the aim to provide a systematic summary of their fabrication, modification, and energy storage applications in lithium-ion batteries, lithium-oxygen batteries, on-chip electrostatic capacitors and micro-supercapacitors.  A comprehensive understanding of the relationship between engineered nanomembranes and electrochem. properties of lithium ion storage with engineered single-tube microbatteries is given, and the flexibility and transparency of micro-supercapacitors is also discussed.  Remarks on challenges and perspectives related to engineered nanomembranes for the further development of energy storage applications conclude this review.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c4cs00218k"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanostructured Mn-based oxides for electrochemical energy storage and conversion</span>. <i>Chem. Soc. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>44</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">699</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">728</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c4cs00218k</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured Mn-based oxides for electrochemical energy storage and conversion</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Kai; Han, Xiaopeng; Hu, Zhe; Zhang, Xiaolong; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">44</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">699-728</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Batteries and supercapacitors as electrochem. energy storage and conversion devices are continuously serving for human life.  The electrochem. performance of batteries and supercapacitors depends in large part on the active materials in electrodes.  As an important family, Mn-based oxides have shown versatile applications in primary batteries, secondary batteries, metal-air batteries, and pseudocapacitors due to their high activity, high abundance, low price, and environmental friendliness.  In order to meet future market demand, it is essential and urgent to make further improvements in energy and power densities of Mn-based electrode materials with the consideration of multiple electron reaction and low mol. wt. of the active materials.  Meanwhile, nanomaterials are favorable to achieve high performance by means of shortening the ionic diffusion length and providing large surface areas for electrode reactions.  This article reviews the recent efforts made to apply nanostructured Mn-based oxides for batteries and pseudocapacitors.  The influence of structure, morphol., and compn. on electrochem. performance has been systematically summarized.  Compared to bulk materials and notable metal catalysts, nanostructured Mn-based oxides can promote the thermodn. and kinetics of the electrochem. reactions occurring at the solid-liq. or the solid-liq.-gas interface.  In particular, nanostructured Mn-based oxides such as one-dimensional MnO2 nanostructures, MnO2-conductive matrix nanocomposites, concn.-gradient structured layered Li-rich Mn-based oxides, porous LiNi0.5Mn1.5O4 nanorods, core-shell structured LiMnSiO4@C nanocomposites, spinel-type Co-Mn-O nanoparticles, and perovskite-type CaMnO3 with micro-nano structures all display superior electrochem. performance.  This review should shed light on the sustainable development of advanced batteries and pseudocapacitors with nanostructured Mn-based oxides.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201090116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cabana, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Monconduit, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Larcher, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Palacin, M. R.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Beyond Intercalation-Based Li-Ion Batteries: The State of the Art and Challenges of Electrode Materials Reacting Through Conversion Reactions</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2010</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>22</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">E170</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">E192</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201090116</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Beyond Intercalation-Based Li-Ion Batteries: the State of the Art and Challenges of Electrode Materials Reacting Through Conversion Reactions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cabana, Jordi; Monconduit, Laure; Larcher, Dominique; Palacin, M. Rosa</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">E170-E192</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This review highlights the recent developments and the future prospects of the use of phases that react through conversion reactions as both cathode and anode materials in Li-ion batteries.  By moving beyond classical intercalation reactions, a variety of low cost compds. with gravimetric specific capacities that are 2-5 times larger than those attained with currently used materials, such as graphite and LiCoO2, can be achieved.  Nonetheless, several factors currently handicap the applicability of electrode materials entailing conversion reactions. Combined with X-ray absorption near-edge structures, our characterization reveals that such 1T-MoSe2 and single-walled carbon nanotubes (abbreviated as 1T-MoSe2/SWCNTs) hybridized structure can provide strong elec. and chem. coupling between 1T-MoSe2 nanosheets and SWCNT film in a form of C-O-Mo bonding, which significantly benefits a high-efficiency electron/ion transport pathway and structural stability, thus directly enabling high-performance lithium storage properties.  In particular, as a flexible and binder-free Li-ion anode, the 1T-MoSe2/SWCNTs electrode exhibits excellent rate capacity, which delivers a capacity of 630 mAh/g at 3000 mA/g.  Meanwhile, the strong C-O-Mo bonding of 1T-MoSe2/SWCNTs accommodates vol. alteration during the repeated charge/discharge process, which gives rise to 89% capacity retention and a capacity of 971 mAh/g at 300 mA/g after 100 cycles.  This synthetic route of a multifunctional MoSe2/SWCNTs hybrid might be extended to fabricate other 2D layer-based flexible and light electrodes for various applications such as electronics, optics, and catalysts.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref22" class="rightTabRefNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2017.09.032"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The electrochemical exploration of double carbon-wrapped Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> : Towards long-time cycling and superior rate sodium-ion battery cathode</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Constructing composite materials with a smart nanostructure, by using various transition metal oxides and carbon carriers as building blocks, is of great importance to develop highly active, economical noble metal-free catalysts for oxygen redn. reaction (ORR).  We have synthesized a novel ternary composite with a special 3D stacked-up nanostructure, composed of Co3O4, Mn3O4 and graphene oxide (GO), via a facile two-step aq. synthesis without adding any structure directing agent.  The composite was characterized by X-ray diffraction, scanning transmission electron microscope, Raman spectroscopy, and XPS.  The results revealed that Mn3O4 nanocrystals had been successfully epitaxially deposited onto the surface of Co3O4 nanoparticles to form Mn3O4-on-Co3O4 nanostructures on surface of the graphene.  In an alk. environment, the Co3O4-Mn3O4/GO composite exhibits much better electrocatalytic activity and durability towards ORR than individual Mn3O4/GO and Co3O4/GO catalysts.  The recorded kinetic c.d. (JK) of O2 redn. for the composite is 2.078 mA/cm2, which is comparable to that of a com. Pt/C (20%) but far exceeding the sum of that obtained from the Co3O4/GO and Mn3O4/GO.  The remarkably improved ORR activity is closely attributed to the enhanced synergy between these two oxides and the graphene, raised by the 3D stacked-up structure in this composite.  The oxide-on-oxide heterostructure comprising Co3O4 and Mn3O4 can promote covalent electron transfer from carbon support to the oxides as a result of the interphase ligand effect between them, which facilitate the ORR kinetics.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A free-standing Co0.85Se nanosheets/graphene (Co0.85Se NSs/G) composite film was developed as a high performance anode material for both lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) by a simple vacuum filtration and thermal redn. process.  The Co0.85Se NSs/G film demonstrates good flexibility, and the Co0.85Se NSs are uniformly anchored on the graphene to form "sheet-on-sheet" nanostructures with strong interfacial interactions.  The hybrid lamellar film demonstrated excellent electrochem. performances when used as a binder-free anode for LIBs and SIBs.  As an anode material for LIBs, the Co0.85Se NSs/G film exhibited a high initial reversible capacity of 680 mA h g-1 at 50 mA g-1 and an excellent cycling stability and rate performance.  The specific capacity of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film shows almost no fading from 0.05 to 0.5 A g-1, and the capacities were maintained at 613.3 and 522.7 mA h g -1 at 1 and 2 A g-1, resp.  When used as an anode for SIBs, the reversible capacity of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film reached up to 388 mA h g-1 with an initial coulombic efficiency as high as 82.5% at 50 mA g-1.  Even at the higher current densities of 1 and 2 A g-1, the reversible capacities remained at 137.5 and 112.4 mA h g-1 after 500 cycles, resp.  The excellent electrochem. performances should be attributed to the special structure of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film.  On one hand, graphene not only provides an efficient elec. conductive network, but also acts as an elastic layer to buffer the volumetric expansion of the Co0.85Se NSs during the discharge/charge process in LIBs/SIBs, which is helpful for enhancing the cycling stability of the Co0.85Se NSs/G film.         </div><div class="casAbstract">High specific capacity and long cycling life of anode materials still remain major challenges in the development of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). The distinguished performances stem from synergetic merits of the morphol., structure, and mechanism of MoP.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The abundant reserve and low cost of sodium have provoked tremendous evolution of Na-ion batteries (SIBs) in the past few years, but their performances are still limited by either the specific capacity or rate capability.  Attempts to pursue high rate ability with maintained high capacity in a single electrode remains even more challenging.  Here, an elaborate self-branched 2-dimensional SnS2 (B-SnS2) nanoarray electrode is designed by a facile hot bath method for Na storage.  This interesting electrode exhibits areal reversible capacity of ∼3.7 mAh/cm2 (900 mAh/g) and rate capability of 1.6 mAh/cm2 (400 mAh/g) at 40 mA/cm2 (10 A/g).         </div><div class="casAbstract">Capacitive energy storage is distinguished from other types of electrochem. energy storage by short charging times and the ability to deliver significantly more power than batteries. The capacitive charge-storage properties of mesoporous films of iso-oriented α-MoO3 are superior to those of either mesoporous amorphous material or nonporous cryst. MoO3.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The advantages of using nanostructured materials for electrochem. energy storage have focused on the benefits assocd. with short path lengths.  However, another contribution, capacitive effects which become increasingly important at nanoscale dimensions, was studied.  Nanocryst. TiO2 (anatase) was studied over a dimensional regime where both capacitive and Li intercalation processes contribute to the total stored charge.  An anal. of the voltammetric sweep data was used to distinguish between the amt. of charge stored by these 2 processes.  At particle sizes &lt;10 nm, capacitive contributions became increasingly important, leading to greater amts. of total stored charge (gravimetrically normalized) with decreasing TiO2 particle size.  The area normalized capacitance is well &gt;100 μF/cm2, confirming that the capacitive contribution was pseudocapacitive.  Also, decreasing the particle size to the nanoscale regime led to faster charge/discharge rates because diffusion-controlled Li ion intercalation was replaced by faradaic reactions which occur at the surface of the material.  The charge storage and kinetic benefits derived from using nanoscale metal oxides provide an interesting direction for the design of materials that offer both power d. and energy d.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.02.086"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Prabakar, S.
J. R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jeong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pyo, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nanoporous hard carbon anodes for improved electrochemical performance in sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>161</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">23</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">31</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.02.086</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanoporous hard carbon anodes for improved electrochemical performance in sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Prabakar, S. J. Richard; Jeong, Jaehyang; Pyo, Myoungho</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">161</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">23-31</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The porosity and morphol. of sucrose-based hard carbon (SHC) was regulated by varying the amt. of bicarbonate salts added during a simple two-stage sintering process.  During the first-stage thermal treatment of sugar at 200°, CO2 liberated from bicarbonate contributed to the pulverization of particles and to the formation of submicron-sized pores.  Na2CO3 entrapped in a precursor matrix also released CO2 during the second-stage sintering at 850°, producing nanometric pores (∼10 nm in diam.).  The excessively high content of bicarbonates, however, resulted in paper-thin graphitic layers with no submicron-sized pores.  These dual roles of bicarbonates produced nanoporous SHC (NSHC) with the submicron-to-nano-sized pores and the largest surface area that was possible for a specific bicarbonate concn.  The optimal nanoporosity of NSHC lent itself to a sharp increase in reversible capacity.  Reversible capacity of 324 and 289 mA h g-1 were obtained for the first and 100th cycles at 20 mA g-1, in contrast to 251 and 213 mA h g-1, resp., for SHC.  The rate capability of NSHC also was enhanced due to a substantial decrease in the charge transfer resistance and a 5-fold increase in the Na+ diffusion coeff.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref56" class="rightTabRefNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit56" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201800080"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ge, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Multidimensional Evolution of Carbon Structures Underpinned by Temperature-Induced Intermediate of Chloride for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1800080</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/advs.201800080</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i19">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.8b01888" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.8b01888</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Raw FTIR data of cobalt acetylacetonate and CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C, cycling performance of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/graphene, CV curves of CoSe<sub>2</sub>/C at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, CV curves of CoSe2/C from 501th to 508th cycles at 1.5 mV s<sup>–2</sup>, and data information of standard XRD peaks (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/suppl_file/am8b01888_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.8b01888/suppl_file/am8b01888_si_001.pdf">am8b01888_si_001.pdf (576.35 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

<script nonce="9318882b2b3f54b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>

<script nonce="9318882b2b3f54b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      function init() {

          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;

        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();
      }

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");
          //If successful then...
          setCookie("gdpr", "true");
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
          //Show error message
          gdprErrorMessage();
          //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
      }

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;
        } else {
          errorStatus = true;
          $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
      }

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

    $(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
  </script>
</p>
-->

                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="9318882b2b3f54b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
